   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Disney+</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       American subscription video streaming service
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>

      <p><b>Disney+</b> (pronounced <b>Disney Plus</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand#Subscription_models" title="Video on demand">subscription video on-demand</a> <a href="/wiki/Over-the-top_media_service" title="Over-the-top media service">over-the-top</a> <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming</a> service owned and operated by the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company#Media_and_Entertainment_Distribution" title="The Walt Disney Company">Media and Entertainment Distribution</a> division of <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-1">[1]</a></sup> The service primarily distributes films and television series produced by <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">The Walt Disney Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Television" title="Walt Disney Television">Walt Disney Television</a>, with the service also advertising content from the company's <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Disney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Partners" title="National Geographic Partners">National Geographic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Star_(Disney%2B)" title="Star (Disney+)">Star</a> brands in particular. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_films" title="List of Disney+ original films">Original films</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_programming" title="List of Disney+ original programming">television series</a> are also distributed on Disney+. In the United States, it doesn't include the Star brand and sits alongside Disney's other streaming platforms – the general programming-oriented <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a> and the sports-oriented <a href="/wiki/ESPN%2B" title="ESPN+">ESPN+</a> – Disney+ focuses on Disney's core brands such as Marvel or Star Wars and family friendly entertainment. </p>
      <p>Disney+ relies on technology developed by <a href="/wiki/Disney_Streaming_Services" title="Disney Streaming Services">Disney Streaming Services</a>, which was originally established as BAMTech in 2015 when it was spun off from <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a> (MLBAM). Disney increased its ownership share of BAMTech to a controlling stake in 2017, and subsequently transferred ownership to DTCI as part of a corporate restructuring in anticipation of Disney's <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" title="Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">acquisition of 21st Century Fox</a>. With BAMTech helping to launch ESPN+ in early 2018, and Disney's streaming distribution deal with <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> ending in 2019, Disney took the opportunity to use technologies being developed for ESPN+ to establish a Disney-branded streaming service that would feature its content. Production of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_films" title="List of Disney+ original films">films</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_programming" title="List of Disney+ original programming">television shows for exclusive release</a> on the platform began in late 2017. </p>
      <p>Disney+ debuted on November 12, 2019, in the United States, Canada, and the Netherlands, and expanded to Australia, New Zealand, and Puerto Rico a week later. It became available in select European countries in March 2020 and in India in April through Disney's <a href="/wiki/Hotstar" title="Hotstar">Hotstar</a> streaming service, which was rebranded as Disney+ Hotstar. Additional European countries received the service in September 2020, with the service expanding to Latin America in November 2020. Upon launch, it was met with positive reception of its content library, but was criticized for technical problems. Alterations made to films and television shows also attracted media attention. Ten million users had subscribed to Disney+ by the end of its first day of operation.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[a]</a></sup> The service had 86.8 million subscribers as of December&nbsp;2, 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Disney%2B&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <p>In late 2015, Disney launched a streaming service in the United Kingdom called DisneyLife to test the streaming market.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> It was replaced by Disney+ on March 24, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2016, Disney acquired a minority stake in <a href="/wiki/BAMTech" class="mw-redirect" title="BAMTech">BAMTech</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spin-off</a> of <a href="/wiki/MLB_Advanced_Media" title="MLB Advanced Media">MLB Advanced Media</a>'s streaming technology business) for $1 billion, with an option to acquire a majority stake in the future. Following the purchase, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> announced plans for an "exploratory [over-the-top] project" based on its technology (<a href="/wiki/ESPN%2B" title="ESPN+">ESPN+</a>) to supplant its existing linear television services.<sup id="cite_ref-variety-disneybam_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-disneybam-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> On August 8, 2017, Disney invoked its option to acquire a controlling stake in BAMTech for $1.58 billion, increasing its stake to 75%. Alongside the acquisition, the company also announced plans for a second, Disney-branded direct-to-consumer service drawing from its entertainment content, which would launch after the company ends its existing distribution agreement with <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> Not long after, Agnes Chu, story and franchise development executive at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering" title="Walt Disney Imagineering">Walt Disney Imagineering</a>, was the first executive appointed for the unit, as senior vice president of content.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> Chu led two projects to launch the new unit. First, Disney needed to verify exactly what content could be physically and legally made available through a streaming service right away, which meant physically reviewing all content in <a href="/wiki/Disney_Vault" title="Disney Vault">Disney's vaults</a> that had not recently undergone <a href="/wiki/Film_preservation" title="Film preservation">restoration</a>, and reviewing "binders of pieces of paper with legal deals" to identify potential obstacles.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvey_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvey-13">[12]</a></sup> Second, Chu met with leaders of Disney's various content-producing divisions to start brainstorming which projects would be appropriate for release on a streaming service rather than in movie theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-Jarvey_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jarvey-13">[12]</a></sup> Chu later left in August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2017, Disney announced its <a href="/wiki/Acquisition_of_21st_Century_Fox_by_Disney" title="Acquisition of 21st Century Fox by Disney">intent to acquire key entertainment assets</a> from <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Fox" title="21st Century Fox">21st Century Fox</a>. Intended to bolster Disney's content portfolio for its streaming products,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> the acquisition was completed on March 20, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2018, it was reported that former <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung</a> executive Kevin Swint had been appointed as the senior vice president and general manager reporting to BAMTech CEO Michael Paull, who leads development.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hwr_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hwr-19">[18]</a></sup> In March 2018, Disney's top level segment division was reorganized with the formation of Disney Direct-to-Consumer and International, which then included BAMTech, which contains "all consumer-facing tech and products".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> In June of the same year, longtime Disney studio marketing chief, Ricky Strauss, was named president of content and marketing, however reporting to chairman of Disney Direct-to-Consumer and International Kevin Mayer.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-22">[21]</a></sup> In January 2019, Fox Television Group COO Joe Earley was named executive vice president of marketing and operations.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> In June 2019, Matt Brodlie was named as senior vice president of international content development.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> In August 2019, Luke Bradley-Jones was hired as senior vice president of direct to consumer and general manager of Disney+ for Europe and Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On November 8, 2018, Disney CEO <a href="/wiki/Bob_Iger" title="Bob Iger">Bob Iger</a> announced that the service would be named Disney+ and that the company was targeting a launch in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusAnnouncement_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusAnnouncement-26">[25]</a></sup> A September launch was reportedly planned,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> but on April 11, 2019, Disney announced that Disney+ would launch on November 12, 2019 in the United States. Disney stated that it planned to roll the service out worldwide over the next two years, targeting Western Europe and Asia-Pacific countries by late 2019 and early 2020, and Eastern Europe and Latin America during 2020. The timing of international launches is subject to the acquisition or expiration of existing streaming rights deals for Disney content.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusLaunch_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusLaunch-28">[27]</a></sup> On August 6, 2019, Iger announced that it will offer a streaming bundle of Disney+, ESPN+, and the ad-supported version of <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a> for $12.99 per month available at launch.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/D23_(Disney)" title="D23 (Disney)">D23 Expo</a> in August 2019, Disney opened subscriptions to Disney+ at a discounted rate for three years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On September 12, 2019, a trial version of Disney+ became available in the Netherlands with limited content available. This testing phase lasted until the official launch on November 12, when trial users were switched to a paid plan.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Disney+ became available for pre-order in September in the United States with a 7-day free trial upon launch.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2019, Disney released a three-and-a-half-hour trailer on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> to showcase their launch lineup.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> It was also reported that Disney would ban advertisements for competitor Netflix from most of its TV platforms, except ESPN.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Disney+ launched on November 12, 2019 Midnight Pacific Time in the announced initial three launch countries.<sup id="cite_ref-dl0_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dl0-37">[36]</a></sup> The services had some issues the first day from logging in (about 33% of the problems), accessing specific content (about 66%), setting up profiles and watch lists. Some of the issues were due to third party devices.<sup id="cite_ref-vty1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vty1-38">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On November 18, 2019, an investigation by <a href="/wiki/ZDNet" title="ZDNet">ZDNet</a> discovered that thousands of users' accounts were hacked using <a href="/wiki/Keystroke_logging" title="Keystroke logging">keystroke logging</a> or info-stealing <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a>. Their email addresses and passwords were changed, "effectively taking over the account and locking the previous owner out", and their login information was put up for sale on the <a href="/wiki/Dark_web" title="Dark web">dark web</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On March 12, 2020, Vanessa Morrison, who previously served as President of <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios#21st_Century_Fox_era" title="20th Century Studios">Fox Family</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Animation" title="20th Century Animation">20th Century Animation</a>, was appointed President of Streaming for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Studios Motion Picture Production</a> and will oversee development and production of Disney+ film content from The <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a> for both <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney Live Action</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Studios</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-steveandvanessa_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steveandvanessa-40">[39]</a></sup> Morrison reports directly to President of Walt Disney Pictures <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bailey" title="Sean Bailey">Sean Bailey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-steveandvanessa_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steveandvanessa-40">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2020, Disney announced a reorganization of their media business with a greater focus on streaming. They are planning to add more content for Disney+ and their other streaming platforms (such as Hulu) in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyHulu_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyHulu-41">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On December 10, 2020, Disney announced that after a year in its launch, they have 86 million subscribers on Disney+.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">[3]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-:3_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-1">[1]</a></sup> They also announced that they are planning to create even more Star Wars and Marvel content on Disney+.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Content">Content</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_programming" title="List of Disney+ original programming">List of Disney+ original programming</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Disney%2B_original_films" title="List of Disney+ original films">List of Disney+ original films</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The service is built around content from Disney's main entertainment studios and film and television library, including <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disneynature" title="Disneynature">Disneynature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucasfilm" title="Lucasfilm">Lucasfilm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Partners" title="National Geographic Partners">National Geographic</a>, and select films from <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Studios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Pictures" title="Hollywood Pictures">Hollywood Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Searchlight_Pictures" title="Searchlight Pictures">Searchlight Pictures</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_Pictures" title="Touchstone Pictures">Touchstone Pictures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusLineup_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusLineup-42">[41]</a></sup> The service will operate alongside <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>, which Disney gained a controlling stake in following the 21st Century Fox purchase.<sup id="cite_ref-disneyFullControl_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-disneyFullControl-43">[42]</a></sup> Bob Iger stated that Disney+ would be focused specifically on family-oriented entertainment (and not carry any <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America_film_rating_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Motion Picture Association of America film rating system">R</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America_film_rating_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Motion Picture Association of America film rating system">NC-17</a> or TV-MA-rated content), and that Hulu would remain oriented towards general entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusAnnouncement_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusAnnouncement-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dl_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dl-45">[44]</a></sup> Hulu will also host Disney+ as an add-on service.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_library">Content library</span></h3> 
      <p>It is suggested that Disney+ has approximately 7,000 television episodes and 500 films,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> including original television series and films from <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freeform_(TV_channel)" title="Freeform (TV channel)">Freeform</a>, and select titles from <a href="/wiki/20th_Television" title="20th Television">20th Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/ABC_Signature" title="ABC Signature">ABC Signature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusLineup_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusLineup-42">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> New releases from 20th Century Studios (including <a href="/wiki/Blue_Sky_Studios" title="Blue Sky Studios">Blue Sky</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Spies_in_Disguise" title="Spies in Disguise">Spies in Disguise</a></i>) will not immediately be available on either Disney+ or <a href="/wiki/Hulu" title="Hulu">Hulu</a>, as the studio has pre-existing output deals with other premium TV/streaming providers (including <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> in the U.S. until 2022,<sup id="cite_ref-HBO_Fox_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HBO_Fox-49">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crave_(TV_network)" title="Crave (TV network)">Crave</a> in Canada<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Group" title="Sky Group">Sky</a> in the UK, Ireland, Italy and Germany). <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Marvel_(film)" title="Captain Marvel (film)">Captain Marvel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dumbo_(2019_film)" title="Dumbo (2019 film)">Dumbo</a></i> (2019), and <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Endgame" title="Avengers: Endgame">Avengers: Endgame</a></i> became the first theatrically released Disney films to stream exclusively on Disney+ within the pay-cable window.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-22">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It was announced that Disney+ would add the first 30 seasons of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> to the service at launch,<sup id="cite_ref-stark_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stark-51">[b]</a></sup> as the series' new exclusive home,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> with season 31 being added on October 2, 2020 in the USA. </p>
      <p>Iger said that Disney+ will eventually host the entire Disney film library, including films currently in the "<a href="/wiki/Disney_Vault" title="Disney Vault">Disney Vault</a>". However, he stated that the controversial <i><a href="/wiki/Song_of_the_South" title="Song of the South">Song of the South</a></i> (1946), which has never been released on home video in its entirety in the U.S., will not be released on the service.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> For unknown reasons, <i><a href="/wiki/Make_Mine_Music" title="Make Mine Music">Make Mine Music</a></i> is not available on the service, making it the only film in the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Disney animated canon</a> not to be included yet.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> Despite being available at launch, at least four films&nbsp;– <i><a href="/wiki/Home_Alone" title="Home Alone">Home Alone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Home_Alone_2:_Lost_in_New_York" title="Home Alone 2: Lost in New York">Home Alone&nbsp;2: Lost in New York</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_On_Stranger_Tides" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides">Pirates of the Caribbean: On Stranger Tides</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield:_A_Tail_of_Two_Kitties" title="Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties">Garfield: A Tail of Two Kitties</a></i>&nbsp;– were removed from the service in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[c]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It was initially unclear whether the first six films of the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> franchise would be available in the United States at the service's launch, as <a href="/wiki/TBS_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="TBS (U.S. TV channel)">TBS</a> held streaming rights through 2024 as part of its cable rights to the franchise,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> but in April 2019, it was announced that the films would be available at launch along with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Force_Awakens" class="mw-redirect" title="The Force Awakens">The Force Awakens</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[d]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rogue_One" title="Rogue One">Rogue One</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup> with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Jedi" class="mw-redirect" title="The Last Jedi">The Last Jedi</a></i> added on December 26, 2019; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rise_of_Skywalker" class="mw-redirect" title="The Rise of Skywalker">The Rise of Skywalker</a></i> added on <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Day" title="Star Wars Day">May 4</a>, 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Solo:_A_Star_Wars_Story" title="Solo: A Star Wars Story">Solo: A Star Wars Story</a></i> was added on July&nbsp;10, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the United States, most of the films from the <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">Marvel Cinematic Universe</a> were available at launch, with the exception of seven films: <i><a href="/wiki/Thor:_Ragnarok" title="Thor: Ragnarok">Thor: Ragnarok</a></i> (added on December 5, 2019), <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Panther_(film)" title="Black Panther (film)">Black Panther</a></i> (added on March 4, 2020), <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Infinity_War" title="Avengers: Infinity War">Avengers: Infinity War</a></i> (added on June 25, 2020), and <i><a href="/wiki/Ant-Man_and_the_Wasp" title="Ant-Man and the Wasp">Ant-Man and the Wasp</a></i> (added on August 14, 2020), due to existing licensing deals with Netflix; and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredible_Hulk_(film)" title="The Incredible Hulk (film)">The Incredible Hulk</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_Homecoming" title="Spider-Man: Homecoming">Spider-Man: Homecoming</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_Far_From_Home" title="Spider-Man: Far From Home">Spider-Man: Far From Home</a></i>, which are unavailable because their distribution rights are owned by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Pictures" title="Universal Pictures">Universal Pictures</a> (<i>The Incredible Hulk</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures" title="Sony Pictures">Sony Pictures</a> (Spider-Man).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Censorship">Censorship</span></h4> 
      <p>Some films were modified for <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> purposes: a post-credits scene from <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_2" title="Toy Story 2">Toy Story 2</a></i> was edited out;<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup> nudity was eliminated from <i><a href="/wiki/Splash_(film)" title="Splash (film)">Splash</a></i> by adding digital hair, blurring, and cropping certain scenes;<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[e]</a></sup> films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Adventures_in_Babysitting" title="Adventures in Babysitting">Adventures in Babysitting</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Free_Solo" title="Free Solo">Free Solo</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Hamilton_(2020_film)" title="Hamilton (2020 film)">Hamilton</a></i>, were altered to remove profanity;<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[f]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Bullwhip_Griffin" title="The Adventures of Bullwhip Griffin">The Adventures of Bullwhip Griffin</a></i> (1967) was edited to remove <a href="/wiki/Racial_slur" class="mw-redirect" title="Racial slur">racial slurs</a>, and the short film <i><a href="/wiki/Santa%27s_Workshop_(film)" title="Santa's Workshop (film)">Santa's Workshop</a></i> (1932) was edited to remove a "<a href="/wiki/Stereotypes_of_African_Americans" title="Stereotypes of African Americans">stereotypical black</a> doll".<sup id="cite_ref-censored_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-73">[68]</a></sup> Many older films and animated shorts have a text disclaimer on the platform noting the possibility of outdated cultural depictions.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[g]</a></sup> Starting in October 2020, a 12-second disclaimer informing viewers of racially insensitive scenes plays before some older Disney films&nbsp;– including <i><a href="/wiki/Peter_Pan_(1953_film)" title="Peter Pan (1953 film)">Peter Pan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dumbo" title="Dumbo">Dumbo</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aristocats" title="The Aristocats">The Aristocats</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[75]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men:_Days_of_Future_Past" title="X-Men: Days of Future Past">X-Men: Days of Future Past</a></i>, which contains both nudity and the <a href="/wiki/%22F%22_word" class="mw-redirect" title="&quot;F&quot; word">"F" word</a>, began airing uncensored in mid-2020.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[76]</a></sup> Some series are missing episodes, including <i><a href="/wiki/Darkwing_Duck" title="Darkwing Duck">Darkwing Duck</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Mermaid_(TV_series)" title="The Little Mermaid (TV series)">The Little Mermaid</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/TaleSpin" title="TaleSpin">TaleSpin</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_and_His_Amazing_Friends" title="Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends">Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-sunfire_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunfire-84">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[h]</a></sup> and <i>The Simpsons</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-wrong_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrong-86">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stark_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stark-51">[b]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[i]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_scripted_content">Original scripted content</span></h3> 
      <p>The service's initial original content goal was planned to include four to five original films and five television shows with budgets from $25–100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-dl_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dl-45">[44]</a></sup> In January 2019, it was reported that Disney would spend up to $500 million in original content for the service.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[j]</a></sup> Original series based on <i>Star Wars</i> and <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel</a> properties have been or are being produced: the former includes <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mandalorian" title="The Mandalorian">The Mandalorian</a></i> (set between <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i> and <i>The Force Awakens</i>), a seventh season of the animated <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(2008_TV_series)" title="Star Wars: The Clone Wars (2008 TV series)">The Clone Wars</a></i>, a successor to the Clone Wars, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_television_series#The_Bad_Batch" title="List of Star Wars television series">Bad Batch</a> a spin-off series focused on <a href="/wiki/Cassian_Andor" title="Cassian Andor">Cassian Andor</a> from <i>Rogue One</i>, as well as one centered on <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Ewan_McGregor" title="Ewan McGregor">Ewan McGregor</a> reprising his role), a series focusing on Ahsoka Tano and a Rangers of the New Republic to intersect with the continuity of <i>The Mandalorian</i><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[82]</a></sup>;<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusAnnouncement_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusAnnouncement-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[83]</a></sup> the latter includes <i><a href="/wiki/WandaVision" title="WandaVision">WandaVision</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Falcon_and_the_Winter_Soldier" title="The Falcon and the Winter Soldier">The Falcon and the Winter Soldier</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Loki_(TV_series)" title="Loki (TV series)">Loki</a></i>, an animated <i><a href="/wiki/What_If...%3F_(TV_series)" title="What If...? (TV series)">What If</a></i> series, <i><a href="/wiki/Ms._Marvel_(TV_series)" title="Ms. Marvel (TV series)">Ms. Marvel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hawkeye_(2021_TV_series)" title="Hawkeye (2021 TV series)">Hawkeye</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Moon_Knight_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moon Knight (TV series)">Moon Knight</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/She-Hulk_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="She-Hulk (TV series)">She-Hulk</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-vty_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vty-94">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marvel3ShowsTHR_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marvel3ShowsTHR-95">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2019, Disney+ ordered <i><a href="/wiki/Diary_of_a_Future_President" title="Diary of a Future President">Diary of a Future President</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/CBS_Television_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="CBS Television Studios">CBS Television Studios</a>, its first series from an outside production company.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A <a href="/wiki/High_Fidelity_(TV_series)" title="High Fidelity (TV series)">television series remake</a> of the film <i><a href="/wiki/High_Fidelity_(film)" title="High Fidelity (film)">High Fidelity</a></i> was initially announced for Disney+, but in April 2019, it was announced that the project had been moved to Hulu, citing concerns from its staff that the positioning of Disney+ as a family-friendly service was at odds with their creative vision for the series.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[87]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Love,_Victor" title="Love, Victor">Love, Victor</a></i>, a spin-off of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Love,_Simon" title="Love, Simon">Love, Simon</a></i>, was similarly shifted from Disney+ to Hulu in February 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2019, Iger announced that 20th Century Fox films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Home_Alone_(franchise)" title="Home Alone (franchise)">Home Alone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Night_at_the_Museum_(film_series)" title="Night at the Museum (film series)">Night at the Museum</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid_(film_series)" title="Diary of a Wimpy Kid (film series)">Diary of a Wimpy Kid</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Cheaper_by_the_Dozen_(2003_film)" title="Cheaper by the Dozen (2003 film)">Cheaper by the Dozen</a></i> will be "'reimagined' for 'a new generation'" exclusively for Disney+<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[89]</a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox#Fox_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="20th Century Fox">Fox Family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[90]</a></sup> Original episodic content will be released weekly, opposed to all at once<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[91]</a></sup> with the release time to be 12:01&nbsp;a.m. PT on Fridays, starting November 15, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On December 25, 2020 <i><a href="/wiki/Soul_(2020_film)" title="Soul (2020 film)">Soul</a></i> became the first feature length film from Pixar to be released as a Disney+ Original. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_unscripted_content">Original unscripted content</span></h3> 
      <p>Disney also plans original factual television content for the service, aiming to "find the ethos of Disney in everyday stories, inspiring hope and sparking the curiosity of audiences of all ages." Some of these series will have ties to Disney properties, including behind-the-scenes documentary miniseries focusing on Disney studios (such as one following the production of <i><a href="/wiki/Frozen_II" title="Frozen II">Frozen II</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-vty_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vty-94">[84]</a></sup> the Disney-themed <a href="/wiki/Competition" title="Competition">competition</a> cooking competition <i>Be Our Chef</i>, <i>Cinema Relics</i> (a documentary series showcasing iconic costume and props from Disney films), <i><a href="/wiki/Hero_Project" title="Hero Project">Marvel's Hero Project</a></i> (a series that will showcase "inspiring kids [that] have dedicated their lives to selfless acts of bravery and kindness"), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Imagineering_Story" title="The Imagineering Story">The Imagineering Story</a></i> (a <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Iwerks" title="Leslie Iwerks">Leslie Iwerks</a>-directed documentary series chronicling the history and work of <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering" title="Walt Disney Imagineering">Walt Disney Imagineering</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-hwr0_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hwr0-103">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vty0_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vty0-104">[94]</a></sup> National Geographic is also producing <i><a href="/wiki/Magic_of_the_Animal_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic of the Animal Kingdom">Magic of the Animal Kingdom</a></i> (a docuseries following the animal caretakers of <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney's Animal Kingdom">Disney's Animal Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Epcot" title="Epcot">Epcot</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Seas_with_Nemo_%26_Friends" title="The Seas with Nemo &amp; Friends">aquarium</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_According_to_Jeff_Goldblum" title="The World According to Jeff Goldblum">The World According to Jeff Goldblum</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Disney reached a two-year pact with the documentary studio Supper Club (Brian McGinn, David Gelb and Jason Sterman, producers of Netflix's <i><a href="/wiki/Chef%27s_Table" title="Chef's Table">Chef's Table</a></i>) to produce content for the service, including the <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation</a>-themed nature documentary series <i>Earthkeepers</i>, and a documentary series chronicling the cultural and societal impact of Marvel's characters. Other factual series include <i><a href="/wiki/Encore!_(TV_series)" title="Encore! (TV series)">Encore!</a></i> (a <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Bell" title="Kristen Bell">Kristen Bell</a>-produced series that reunites casts from high school musical productions to reprise their roles), <i><a href="/wiki/(Re)Connect" class="mw-redirect" title="(Re)Connect">(Re)Connect</a></i> (a reality series produced by <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Ripa" title="Kelly Ripa">Kelly Ripa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Consuelos" title="Mark Consuelos">Mark Consuelos</a>' Milojo Productions), <i>Rogue Trip</i> (a travel series featuring <a href="/wiki/Bob_Woodruff" title="Bob Woodruff">Bob Woodruff</a> and his son Mack), and the reality competition <i>Shop Class</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-hwr0_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hwr0-103">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vty0_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vty0-104">[94]</a></sup> On December 3, 2019, Disney+ announced the new <i>Star Wars</i>-based children's <a href="/wiki/Game_show" title="Game show">game show</a> <i>Jedi Temple Challenge</i> to be hosted by Ahmed Best, who voiced <a href="/wiki/Jar_Jar_Binks" title="Jar Jar Binks">Jar Jar Binks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_prequel_trilogy" title="Star Wars prequel trilogy">prequel trilogy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Device_support_and_service_features">Device support and service features</span></h2> 
      <p>Disney+ is available for streaming via web browsers on PC and Mac, as well as apps on Apple <a href="/wiki/IOS_device" class="mw-redirect" title="IOS device">iOS devices</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> mobile devices and <a href="/wiki/Android_TV" title="Android TV">Android TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> devices such as <a href="/wiki/Fire_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire TV">Fire TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fire_HD" title="Fire HD">Fire HD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromecast" title="Chromecast">Chromecast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromebook" title="Chromebook">Chromebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Smart_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Samsung Smart TV">Samsung smart TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/LG_Smart_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="LG Smart TV">LG smart TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vizio" class="mw-redirect" title="Vizio">Vizio SmartCast TVs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roku" title="Roku">Roku</a> devices, <a href="/wiki/Sky_Q" title="Sky Q">Sky Q</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Now_TV_(Sky)" title="Now TV (Sky)">Now TV</a> devices,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[98]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_5" title="PlayStation 5">PlayStation 5</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Series_X_and_Series_S" title="Xbox Series X and Series S">Xbox Series X/S</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Windows_10" title="Windows 10">Windows 10</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[100]</a></sup> Content available on Disney+ is also listed in the <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV_app" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple TV app">Apple TV app</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTCI_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTCI-111">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Accessibility" title="Accessibility">Accessibility</a> features include <a href="/wiki/Closed_captioning" title="Closed captioning">closed captioning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Descriptive_Video_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Descriptive Video Service">Descriptive Video Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Audio_description" title="Audio description">audio description</a>, and audio navigation assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Disney+ allows seven user profiles per account, with the ability to stream on four devices concurrently and unlimited downloads for offline viewing. Content is able to be streamed in resolutions up to <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K</a> <a href="/wiki/Ultra-high-definition_television" title="Ultra-high-definition television">Ultra HD</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Vision" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolby Vision">Dolby Vision</a> and <a href="/wiki/HDR10" class="mw-redirect" title="HDR10">HDR10</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Atmos" title="Dolby Atmos">Dolby Atmos</a> sound on supported devices. Legacy content is available in English, Spanish, French, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, while Disney+ originals features additional language options.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[103]</a></sup> Subtitles and dubbing are available in up to 16 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[104]</a></sup> A substantial amount of content is available in Hindi, Indonesian, Tamil and Telugu languages on the Indian and Indonesian counterpart, Disney+Hotstar.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In late May 2020, the service added the ability to switch between 4:3 and 16:9 aspect ratios for early <i>Simpsons</i> episodes,<sup id="cite_ref-AspectRatioFeature_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AspectRatioFeature-116">[106]</a></sup> after the service received backlash for stretching those episodes to 16:9 by default at launch.<sup id="cite_ref-SimpsonsAspectRatio_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SimpsonsAspectRatio-117">[107]</a></sup> Disney had done this "in order to guarantee visual quality and consistency across all 30 seasons." To accommodate the feature, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Streaming_Services" title="Disney Streaming Services">Disney Streaming Services</a> "had to reconfigure its content-delivery engine" while ensuring the new feature would not break any existing features such as continue watching, watchlists, and auto-playing, as they did not want to treat the 4:3 versions as bonus content. The resulting changes allowed Disney to apply the existing audio, subtitle information, episode artwork, and other metadata from the episodes to both aspect ratios regardless of which is chosen by the user. Joe Rice, vice president of media product at Disney Streaming Services, added that these adjustments "opens up a number of exciting opportunities for novel ways of presenting content in the future."<sup id="cite_ref-AspectRatioFeature_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AspectRatioFeature-116">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2020, the service added the GroupWatch feature which allows up to seven different Disney+ accounts to link up and co-view programming with one another. Viewers are able to react to content with six different emojis, and control playback for the entire group. It is available on web browser, mobile app, smart TVs, and connected TV devices in the United States, and will expand to Europe later in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[108]</a></sup> The feature was previously tested in Australia, Canada, and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch">Launch</span></h2> 
      <p>Disney+ was launched early in the Netherlands on September 12, 2019 as a free trial. It officially launched in the Netherlands, United States and Canada on November 12, 2019 just before 3:00&nbsp;a.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Standard_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Standard Time">EST</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%E2%88%9205:00" title="UTC−05:00">UTC–5</a>). Disney+ launched in Australia, New Zealand, and Puerto Rico on November 19, 2019, and launched in Austria, the United Kingdom, Spain, Italy, Germany, Ireland, and Switzerland on March 24, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusLaunch_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusLaunch-28">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnet_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnet-120">[110]</a></sup> In the UK and Ireland, Disney+ replaced DisneyLife. In Spain, a linear Disney+ TV channel launched alongside the streaming service, which broadcasts programming from Disney+. It's available exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Movistar%2B" title="Movistar+">Movistar+</a>, their release partner in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Movistar_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Movistar-121">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2019, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Groupe_Canal%2B" title="Groupe Canal+">Canal+</a> would be the exclusive distributor of Disney+ in France.<sup id="cite_ref-CanalPlus_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CanalPlus-122">[112]</a></sup> The launch in France was delayed from March 24 to April 7, pursuant to a request from the French government to conserve network capacity due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> placing additional strain on communications networks.<sup id="cite_ref-FranceReport_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FranceReport-123">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2020, Iger announced that it planned to launch Disney+ in India on March 29, 2020 by means of its existing service <a href="/wiki/Hotstar" title="Hotstar">Hotstar</a>, rebranding its paid tiers as a co-branded service. Hotstar was acquired by Disney during the Fox purchase, and has been the dominant streaming service in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[115]</a></sup> However, it was postponed due to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Premier_League" title="Indian Premier League">Indian Premier League</a> being rescheduled due to the COVID-19 pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusPostponed_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusPostponed-126">[116]</a></sup> It was then launched on April 3, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-DisneyPlusIndia_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DisneyPlusIndia-127">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2020, it was announced that Disney+ original content would be licensed to pay TV and streaming operator <a href="/wiki/OSN" title="OSN">OSN</a>, starting on April 9, in 17 countries in the <a href="/wiki/MENA" title="MENA">Middle East and North Africa region</a> with Disney noting that they had no current "plan to launch Disney+ as a standalone service in the region in the near future".<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The service launched in Japan on June 11, 2020 as part of Disney's existing partnership with <a href="/wiki/NTT_Docomo" title="NTT Docomo">NTT Docomo</a>, and succeeded the existing <a href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E3%83%87%E3%82%A3%E3%82%BA%E3%83%8B%E3%83%BC%E3%83%87%E3%83%A9%E3%83%83%E3%82%AF%E3%82%B9" class="extiw" title="jp:ディズニーデラックス">Disney Deluxe</a> service in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-131">[121]</a></sup> Disney+ launched in Indonesia through <a href="/wiki/Hotstar" title="Hotstar">Hotstar</a> on September 5, 2020;<sup id="cite_ref-IndonesiaLaunch_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndonesiaLaunch-132">[122]</a></sup> Portugal, Belgium, Finland, Iceland, Luxembourg, Norway, Sweden, Denmark, and Greenland<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[123]</a></sup> on September 15, 2020;<sup id="cite_ref-PortugalLaunch_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PortugalLaunch-134">[124]</a></sup> and in Latin America and the Caribbean on November 17, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-LatinAmericaLaunch_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LatinAmericaLaunch-135">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On December 10, 2020, Disney announced that the service would expand to Singapore on February 23, 2021,<sup id="cite_ref-CNA_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNA-136">[126]</a></sup> and to Eastern Europe, South Korea, and Hong Kong sometime in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-EESKHKLaunch_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EESKHKLaunch-137">[127]</a></sup> It was also announced that the same day, Disney+ will also begin offering general entertainment content in Canada, Europe, Australia, New Zealand, South Korea, Hong Kong and Singapore via the branded portal <a href="/wiki/Star_(Disney%2B)" title="Star (Disney+)">Star</a> in select international markets (taking its branding from Disney's pay television businesses in Asia). Similarly to Hulu, Star will include films and series from the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Television" title="Walt Disney Television">Walt Disney Television</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Studios" title="20th Century Studios">20th Century Studios</a> libraries that fall outside of Disney's core franchises (including ABC, <a href="/wiki/FX_(TV_channel)" title="FX (TV channel)">FX</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Freeform_(TV_channel)" title="Freeform (TV channel)">Freeform</a> programs).<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[129]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright" style="">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:fit-content; width:-moz-fit-content; width:-webkit-fit-content;">
        <div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:auto;">
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r950958020">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output div.mw-graph{min-width:auto!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style>
         <div class="mw-graph" style="min-width:480px;min-height:150px">
          <img class="mw-graph-img" src="/api/rest_v1/page/graph/png/Disney%2B/0/8d03f6c3405d815562b96a17ec4e96d361496fe6.png">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         Evolution of worldwide subscribers of Disney+<sup id="cite_ref-10MSubs_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10MSubs-161">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Subs2020Q1_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subs2020Q1-162">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50MSubs_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50MSubs-163">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SubsMay2020_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SubsMay2020-164">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SubsAugust2020_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SubsAugust2020-165">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73Million_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73Million-166">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86Million_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86Million-167">[152]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On November 13, 2019, a day after its launch, Disney announced that the streaming service had already signed up more than 10 million subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-10MSubs_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10MSubs-161">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[153]</a></sup> Disney+ has been well-received, thanks to its affordable price and for the extensive Disney library. Frank Pallotta of <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> stated that "the company [Disney] has repackaged its trove of beloved content for the service makes it a worthy companion to the other services in the marketplace.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[154]</a></sup> Nick Pino of <i><a href="/wiki/TechRadar" title="TechRadar">TechRadar</a></i> stated, "If Disney keeps it updated with new content, Disney+ could rival Netflix sooner rather than later."<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Upon launch, Disney+ experienced significant technical difficulties. Users complained about receiving error messages that the service was down and that they were "unable to connect", which were irritating because many of them had paid for the service months in advance.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[156]</a></sup> In some instances, passwords needed to be reset to enable access. </p>
      <p>One other negative aspect with the launch of the service was the presentation of the non-HD episodes of <i>The Simpsons</i>. Namely, that instead of presenting them in their original aspect ratio, they were either cropped to fit <a href="/wiki/16:9" class="mw-redirect" title="16:9">16:9</a> widescreen televisions or awkwardly stretched out to that aspect ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-SimpsonsAspectRatio_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SimpsonsAspectRatio-117">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/FXX" title="FXX">FXX</a>'s now-defunct "Simpsons World" streaming service was similarly criticized when it launched.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[157]</a></sup> In response, Disney stated they would make the ability to watch the episodes of the first 19 seasons and some from season 20 in either the 4:3 or 16:9 aspect ratio in early 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[158]</a></sup> The feature was made available on May 28, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-AspectRatioFeature_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AspectRatioFeature-116">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some have noted that episodes of <i>The Simpsons</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_(TV_series)" title="X-Men (TV series)">X-Men</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/DuckTales_(2017_TV_series)" title="DuckTales (2017 TV series)">DuckTales</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Phineas_and_Ferb" title="Phineas and Ferb">Phineas and Ferb</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kim_Possible" title="Kim Possible">Kim Possible</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers:_Earth%27s_Mightiest_Heroes" title="The Avengers: Earth's Mightiest Heroes">The Avengers: Earth's Mightiest Heroes</a></i> are presented almost entirely out of order, while some series are missing episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-collider_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collider-174">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wrong_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrong-86">[78]</a></sup> Others have questioned why an extensive catalog of Disney-owned material is missing from the platform, including Marvel content,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[161]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disney_Junior" title="Disney Junior">Disney Junior</a> titles,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[162]</a></sup> various <a href="/wiki/Muppets" class="mw-redirect" title="Muppets">Muppets</a> media,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[163]</a></sup> and <i>Star Wars</i> <span class="nowrap">spin-offs</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[166]</a></sup> On June 26, 2020, the 2017 <i>DuckTales</i> series had its episodes arranged in the proper order while co-creator of <i>Phineas and Ferb</i>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_%22Swampy%22_Marsh" title="Jeff &quot;Swampy&quot; Marsh">Jeff "Swampy" Marsh</a>, has stated that they are working on correcting the order of his series.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Disney+ was the top trending <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google</a> search term in 2019 in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[168]</a></sup> In February 2020, Disney reported that Disney+ had 26.5 million subscribers by the end of 2019, and 28.6 million by February 3, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Subs2020Q1_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Subs2020Q1-162">[147]</a></sup> By April, Disney+ had 50 million paid subscribers, with approximately 8 million of those coming from India.<sup id="cite_ref-50MSubs_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50MSubs-163">[148]</a></sup> The service had 54.5 million subscribers by May 4,<sup id="cite_ref-SubsMay2020_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SubsMay2020-164">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[169]</a></sup> 57.5 million subscribers by the end of June, 60.5 million subscribers by August 4,<sup id="cite_ref-SubsAugust2020_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SubsAugust2020-165">[150]</a></sup> 73.7 million subscribers by September 30,<sup id="cite_ref-73Million_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73Million-166">[151]</a></sup> and 86.8 million subscribers as of December 2.<sup id="cite_ref-86Million_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86Million-167">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2020, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> named Disney+ the <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a> App of the Year. It was the second and third most-downloaded free app of the year globally on the <a href="/wiki/IPad" title="IPad">iPad</a> and <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, respectively. It was also voted the best app of 2020 by <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a> users.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[170]</a></sup> </p>

         <li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The rights to <i>The Force Awakens</i> (among various other Disney films) are owned by the premium television network <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz</a> (as they have previously been the first-run pay-TV provider for Walt Disney Studios' releases between 1994 and 2015).          <li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-75">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Words like "<a href="/wiki/Fuck" title="Fuck">fuck</a>", "goddamn", and "homo" were censored from <i>Adventures in Babysitting</i> and <i>Free Solo</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-censored_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-censored-73">[68]</a></sup> however, <i>Hamilton</i> retained one instance of "fuck" as that is allowed in a <a href="/wiki/PG-13" class="mw-redirect" title="PG-13">PG-13</a> film.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[69]</a></sup></span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One episode featuring <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> imagery and (Nazi agent <a href="/wiki/Red_Skull" title="Red Skull">Red Skull</a>) was omitted. Additionally, the series' third episode features a warning about racially insensitive content regarding stereotypes of Asians.<sup id="cite_ref-sunfire_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunfire-84">[77]</a></sup></span> </li>

                  <ul>
